Saturday 20190928 weight 15?.? 50? bpm @ 5:0? > 32F @ 5:15 (Mt. Taylor)
did not know weight because did not take scale

5:15 wake-up
10 double espresso

5:30 Pre-race calories
533 fortified oatmeal
0 200 mg ibuprofen

6:15 pre-race caffeine
20 quad espresso

During the Mt Taylor 50k I chose to have a single 20 oz. handheld,
which I initially had loaded with 2 scoops of Tailwind and 2
tablespoons of chia.  I also had a baggie with another (2 scoops of
Tailwind and 2 tablespoons of chia) setup and a baggie with just 2
tablespoons of chia.  When I ran out of my first set of liquid, I got
water at an aid station and mixed up my baggie that had Tailwind, then
for the rest of the race I always put aid-station-provided Tailwind in
my bottle, except at the 1/2 way point where I had already mixed 2
scoops of my own with 2 tablespoons of chia and water.  I *meant* to
take more baggies of just 2 tablespoons of chia, but I got flustered
at the aid station and forgot to grab them and also forgot initially
to take my quad espresso.

I had too much emergency gear in my 1/2 way drop bag.  I should have
stripped it, especially since I also had access to my finisher's bag.
I need to always have a printed list of the things I need to switch
out; it only takes a few seconds to read such a list.

BTW, taking all that espresso, ibuprofen and chocolate left my stomach
slightly sore, but I don't think that really held me back.  I think a
combination of injury and still not being 100% recovered from Big
Cottonwood held me back much more.  I also knew Eric Pope was gunning
for the 56 year old record and I knew I didn't have it in me to beat
him, so I took my foot off the gas and had a great day.

Although I wrote down some of the calorie sources I was bringing with
me, I didn't write down what I ate post race until the following day.

Tuesday 20191022 weight 159.9 39 bpm @ 4:50 44.2F @ 8:38 (Heritage Hills)
https://www.wunderground.com/weather/us/nm/albuquerque/KNMALBUQ429
51.4F 20 minutes after (forgot to record it)

Today was an experiment, in that on the Tuesday after DCM and before
JJ100 last year, I ran my 8.9 miles much later in the day and after a
bunch of calories.  I started later after a false start where I
returned very early due to lightning.

Today, to some extent I tried to eat similarly (although last time
there were homemade calzones) and ran at 8:40 to see just how quickly
I can run my standard 8.9 mile (to Albuquerque Academy, two loops
around, and back) Tuesday run at 130bpm.  It wouldn't have been a fair
comparison due to differences in temperature, humidity and wind
anyway, but I was getting some pretty heavy HR swings that makes me
think I can't trust the numbers at all.

FWIW, I *felt* great.  If I had known that I wouldn't trust the HR
results, I would have just chosen a pace around 9 minutes a mile and
held on to it to see if I could do that with the same feeling as a
130bpm HR.  Oh well.  I can do interval training tomorrow and then
compare my non-HR interval stats with those from interval training
yesterday and figure out if yesterday's and today's trainings were net
*short term* wins (I'm sure they were worthwhile overall).

Monday 20191209 weight 15?.? ?? @ ?:?? 30F @ 1:00 (top of crest, car thermometer)

I got called out on a search-and-rescue mission at about 11:30 Sunday
night.  I got out the door at about midnight and got to the top of the
crest just slightly after 1am.  I could not get the Sienna to the
parking spaces at the top, but Jesse helped me at least get the
Sienna to a safe place out of the way.

I was a useful member of team one, although Jesse and Bill led the
way, with Jesse doing trail finding.  The subject was a little below
the stairs on the Crest Trail Spur.  We went down in our snowshoes,
but should have used micro-spikes instead.

I mostly carried stuff, then, after the subject was safely in an
ambulance, I misplaced my keys and wound up going back (by that time
it was daylight) to look for them.  It's a bit of a long story, but I
was convinced my keys were with my phone and they weren't.  My phone
had slid off the console presumably when the Sienna was slipping and
sliding up at the top and out of sight is out of mind, so my keys were
in a baggie by themselves and I later repurposed that baggie to hold
various Jet Boil parts because I didn't have time or finger
coordination to get the Jet Boil back into a cohesive unit (and the
baggie that normally held the Jet Boil had been repurposed).

Anyway, I wound up eating 3 gels while the subjeft was being attended
to, not because I needed calories, per-se, but because I let my
fingers get very cold (because I had switched to my very warm, but
totally awkward mittens, but that meant I had to take my hands out of
the mittens completely to do a bunch of tasks, including repeatedly
handling the subject's completely frozen pants and shoes that I had
volunteered to schlep about.

Altuough I was wearing my Ambit 3, I must have either accidentally
turned it off when I thought I was locking the controls or turned it
off when getting into my pack and then forgot to lock it (or perhaps I
locied it after turning it off).  So, my exercise log has guesses for
that activity.  Normally I don't write down much detail in this file
for SAR missions because my saved exercise data reminds me what I
did...

FWIW, the subject was taken to the firehouse down the mountain and I
had to go there to retrieve some of the clothing I had lent him.  So I
got to see that he did not get any frostbite.  He still had some
tingling in his toes, but he could feel all of them which was *MUCH*
better than when we found him.  Yay!
